After having played the game for about 60 hours, I simply can't recommend it. While the first few hours do feel great, the decline in quality, especially regarding side activities, is so grueling that I lost every reason to keep playing. The dialogues are cringe af, there's almost no depth to anything and Hogwarts feels completely empty and almost pointless after a while. Besides that - and this is actually my main reason - they still didn't fix the technical issues. Actually, they got worse. I can't keep 60FPS with DLSS at medium settings with a 3060Ti, Ryzen 5 5600X and 32GB RAM. I can literally play Cyberpunk on highest settings with low Raytracing enabled, it looks 10x as good and runs smooth like butter. Not only do I feel like Hogwarts Legacy lacks almost any graphical fidelity (especially characters), there's absolutely no reason for it to run so poorly. I have only been playing for a few days on Xbox one, but I am impressed by some things and not impressed by others. I grew up playing the old Harry Potter games. I have read the whole series several times, and I used to have the first 2 movies memorized, so I would say that I am a Harry Potter fan. To me this did not feel like Hogwarts. The exterior of the castle looked like Hogwarts, but the interior does not feel nor look like Hogwarts in my opinion. I was disappointed that you cannot talk to characters unless they are part of a quest. What is the point of having an open world? I thought that the story line was weak. I thought that it would have been better to start as a first year and work your way up to a seventh year like Harry did. I was really disappointed that there was no Quidditch in the game. Even the old Harry Potter games had Quidditch. In the books AND the movies there was no surrounding town near Hogwarts. Hogwarts was protected by an enchanted fence and then there was Hogsmeade and that was it. They added additional things in there that I thought were unnecessary, but they probably did it as a dig towards JK Rowing because of her stance at the time. A little summary of negative reviews on steam: 1) Heavy compatability issues with PC for many people, even with the highest level pc and screen. 2) Open world is limited by level barriers, so not really very open world 3) NPCs dont react at all to you unless they're part of a quest 4) Normal story is ok, but side stories are very basic and repetitive fetch quests.  5) The limited amount of spells, like 25 in total and 4 at a time, is a bit crippling for the literal wizard world. Do i just forget all the spells i know? 6) Difficulty increase just increases hp and damage, somewhat unfortunately.  7) Overall lack of interactivity with the world and NPCs can make the game seem rather dead.    Overall a solid game, if you're a HP fan it might be worth it. The execution is pretty good. If you're not super-invested in harry potter, the game offers little genre-breaking things.  Free, or cheaper? Sure, worth a shot. But it's 70$. You can buy a lot of good games with that. I'd instead recommend Divinity Original Sin 2 Definitive Edition.

I beat the game in 25 hours, not that that is a bad thing, I love this game, and will probably put a few more in to get more challenges done and explore. The only gripes I have are small gripes as this game has done far far faaar more good than bad. Don't take these as reasons not to buy the game, I totally recommend it, and my cons are minor compared to the rest of this wonderful game. But I will list a few of the cons I have:  - Basic quality of life being locked behind talent points like extra spell (skill) sets. There is no good reason lore or gameplay wise where those should be locked behind precious talent points  - Lack of talent points. In my 25 hours of play, I explored a lot, and didn't get anywhere near the max level 40, and even if you get max level, you can't afford all the talents. I was level 30  - The level system isn't super necessary, I didn't have to grind because my grind was having fun exploring, but you gain levels much much slower into the mid 20s. The talent points could have been attributed through gameplay challenges rather than grinding pages. And since there is no new game plus to experience the different houses you have to do the grind for each house. The first playthrough wasn't a problem, I don't want to go through that again though.   - The gear was more cumbersome than worth it. I ended up not caring after getting 'legendary' gear around level 23-25 and it carried me the rest of the game, turned into busywork and the gear progression was entirely random, but since enemies level with you you need to have decent gear upgrades through most of the game.   - Too many systems that seemed over bearing and worthless. There is the whole beast capturing, caring, and slot system with the loom that I never touched outside of the 2 quests that used it. I never felt like I needed it in the slightest, and it was a lot of time sink that wasn't worth it for me. The potions where almost as useless as you get a never ending supply of healing pots. I only used it for focus potions at the end so I could spam curses.  - You don't get brooms till 25% in the game, and beast mounts until 60%+ in, one of the mounts you don't get until the second last quest and you use it for maybe 2 minutes.   - I avada kedavra'd a boss near the end of the game it emptied his health bar from 97% to 0%, but the devs didn't plan for the killing curse and he lived canonically. immersion broken, 0/10 game, do not buy.

I started a few hours ago, and hot damn... I am loving it.  As he stated, there are some nitpicks for seasoned gamers here and there, but nothing that is anything more than a minor annoyance...far superseded by the incredible attention to detail of the castle, the immersive nature of what is happening, the music, the feeling of mystery, the insanely good graphics (honestly some of the best, if not THE best lighting I have seen in a game), really solid combat, and controls that feel great overall. The gripes about facial animations are definitely overblown. There are times when it is a bit wibbly, but I was actually quite impressed by the mouth movement to mimic actual words so often that I questioned a couple of times whether it was actually mo-capped or not. I was also pleasantly surprised by how much my player character emotes and likewise their facial animation is quite satisfactory, giving them a personality much more obvious than the wooden nature of what is seen in the preview content. Overall, everything I could have hoped for so far.  Wandering the castle currently, lost as shit, and there was no place I would rather be.   Buckle up.

I think there's a way they could implement a 'school schedule' without hurting the game speed/adding more mechanics similar to Bully.  A non-invasive, lorefriendly and voluntairily way would be to let you go to class to "speed up time" and "pretend to have class". I'll explain this.   Later in the game, there might not be much more to do besides exploring. But you still might want to enjoy being a student. So, you'll walk to a classroom, walk towards your usual lectern and press the button prompt that appears. It says: "Attend class". You'll get a short cutscene, time progresses by 3 in-game hours, and you'll continue your day or go to the next class to do this again. In the evening you'll get this same button type prompt at your bedside, saying: "end the day".   Even though you wouldn't get the same school system such as in Bully, as in not a school simulator, it would very much feel like one. This would make a lot of people happy, including me.   One thing I'm always afraid of in games is either the Fallout New Vegas style, or the Far Cry 6 style. Either you can't do anything after the main quest ends, which sends you back in time. Or after doing every quest/location, the world becomes empty and dry. Having such a school system thing in place makes it feel like your character has a daily life, something to do after the end-game.  Side-note: I would also enjoy an option in the game that lets you pick (after the main quest has ended) in which season you want to play in. Maybe you rushed through summer and didn't explore outside as much, or maybe you missed an interesting easter egg during the winter, or you feel like going back to the start of autumn because it just looks so good. This would add a lot of replayability/freedom and make your time exploring more enjoyable. Especially since weather and seasons move dynamically, you might end up missing something because of that.

On the other hand I think it is a bit disappointing that you just gloss over the controversy around the Harry Potter universe with a "there was much arguing" and a general ask to remain civil in the comment section. I do believe that falls a bit flat, to be honest.   I know it is hard between the loud and upset Twitter crowd that wants the books burned on the one hand and the ignorant bigots who just don't consider trans folks to be people at all on the other hand to have somewhat of a constructive discussion about the political and, frankly, ethical dimension of our hobby and our consumption choices. I personally think I will sit this one out for the moral reason, but I wouldn't judge anyone to be excited about a (apparently well produced) Harry Potter game. I'd just ask people to not just yadda yadda over question of basic human rights and the dignity of marginalized groups. I honestly do believe that the gaming scene has a real problem with civil discourse in general, and a channel like you could be a reasonable attempt to create a better conversation about games.
